The CBP's National Air Operations Center -- Corpus Christi building.
 
 
 
 
[Date]2014-06-30      How the Air Force hardens planes against signal leakage 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/d4ef7f8c-d652-4a76-b6f8-870f670e789d/thumbnail/770x578/1f1a1e0027fbb8ecf32e7f6cda537fc9/c-5-nose-up-with-van.jpg
Working out of a special white RV parked alongside a C-5 -- the Air Force's largest airplane -- technicians demonstrated how they test for leaked signals.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/7fc406c4-ed89-431a-9f20-b6d43e2857fa/thumbnail/770x578/ab826f366bc51742f225fbb089d1c125/c-5-nose-up.jpg
The Lockheed C-5 Galaxy is the Air Force's largest airplane, a cargo plane capable of being refueled in mid-air. Cargo can be loaded from either the front, or the rear.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/d569e90f-4d40-4543-8c65-85fbc65450c2/thumbnail/770x578/192fca2c37899f929fd5642c674a026e/c-5.jpg
The C-5, manufactured by Lockheed since 1968, has to be "re-glassed," or revamped, after years of service. When that happens, the 24th Air Force has to make sure all its new or reconfigured communications systems are hardened against unintentional leakage.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/64caf1ab-4273-4980-ba96-6b2290d22342/thumbnail/770x578/5bd5469761a29216316f4b4dad813932/van-and-the-c-5.jpg
The special RV used to monitor communications emissions from Air Force aircraft. The RV can be flown around the world, as the Air Force works to test every aircraft the service flies.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/9617084b-155a-4b8d-9228-4cd9c35ec392/thumbnail/770x578/0c8cc23efaebd3350eb8f605a79ffac2/the-e.jpg
As a demonstration, a laptop aboard the C-5 was set up with this "E" on its screen. The idea was to see if the monitors in the RV could "see" the signal.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/586d8f25-4dca-48b1-8840-26cbdeeac131/thumbnail/770x578/cf4e3694b416d47a0d033a648ba2132e/antenna-and-computer.jpg
A special antenna was set up alongside the laptop, in order to see whether the signal from the computer could be read in the nearby RV.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/e37683f3-0b79-40df-96c0-609dc4a08222/thumbnail/770x578/e643c35e6df5a86e98d3ea15090db60b/ghost-of-the-e.jpg
In the RV, a technician caught an image of the "E," appearing almost ghost-like in a sea of electronic noise. The point was made: the laptop on the plane was not secure enough to be used without stricter security measures.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/edb50ac4-22f1-487a-b6e2-540b29217bb4/thumbnail/770x578/389d0c4bb566704f3d220bfb34fdb7fa/monitoring.jpg
Two Air Force technicians in the RV monitor the signal coming from the laptop on board the C-5.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/0b1c2f89-9724-4df4-af91-85a7ee137819/thumbnail/770x578/98367821f23455f25f7c45036fb7d1a8/c-5-rear-upper-deck.jpg
The double-decker C-5 is 247 feet long, and its upper deck, behind the flight deck, is longer than some other entire airplanes.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/e2db5162-f9e7-4f8b-877d-a6dcc4e6ca46/thumbnail/770x578/70614941c4c706014f07ddcacb5e64d3/interior-main-deck-of-c-5.jpg
A look into the lower deck of a giant Lockheed C-5 Galaxy. The plane is said to be able to fit at least six Greyhound buses.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/27/ac1b12bf-bf2d-4286-9ac6-c115aa8e24a5/thumbnail/770x578/5c0ea537b54815b1053ee1c5abfd1ab3/c-5-flight-deck.jpg
The flight deck of the Lockheed C-5 Galaxy.
 
 
 
[Date]2014-07-01     In Austin, Prof. Dumpster lives the good life 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/09766182-f9bd-4acb-9c97-1b0958620f0f/thumbnail/770x578/07f12d78321543f88ef9ff35a93e473f/exodus.jpg
Professor Dumpster is in the middle of a project meant to prove it's possible to live super minimally, and super efficiently.For a year, Professor Dumpster is living in a 33-square-foot dumpster -- outfitted, of course, for civilized living.
 
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/1d18a681-52c0-4f9f-8db5-1512b7716e8a/thumbnail/770x578/5e976186c82f34f055d9aaa0a0ac05fb/dumpster-axon-phase-3.png
Currently, the Dumpster Project is in Phase I, and Professor Dumpster and his team are actively trying to raise money to proceed to the next stages of the initiative.This document shows what the project is intended to look like when it's much further along. With multiple stories, and a developed garden, this dumpster could be sophisticated living for the minimalist-inclined.
 
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/d62cb2e4-d8d0-401d-a55f-5d034dd3ad75/thumbnail/770x578/aa4a7764fbd0821608a376453abdbb24/prof-dumpster-laughing.jpg
Standing inside the dumpster, located at Huston Tillotson University in Austin, Texas, Jeffrey Wilson, aka Professor Dumpster, laughs and enjoys his 33-square-foot home.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/ac59132c-413d-4fe3-bc9f-71ed94a6313f/thumbnail/770x578/9eb7bce14ce4c7c1fc7dbe6f498afe6a/pushing-water-tank.jpg
In its current state, the dumpster isn't connected to the grid in any way, which means that Professor Dumpster must get water the old-fashioned way -- by carrying it home. When he needs water, he pushes this water barrel, which holds 24 gallons, to Austin's Lady Bird Lake, an hour round-trip, where he fills it up. When he returns, he filters the water in order to make it potable.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/f3f60272-e7aa-4a0b-8d30-f598b4990102/thumbnail/770x578/656d90cbaceed329071378065b26cec4/on-the-phone.jpg
Though the dumpster isn't connected to the grid, that doesn't mean Professor Dumpster is cut off from the world. He uses his iPhone to talk to people, and he spends much of the daylight hours at his university office, which is only a couple hundred yards away.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/69c76f73-05fc-43f9-96fc-c737d5bd5cb1/thumbnail/770x578/06550991c0b269586a2a40abbf2f58dc/second-layer-in-hidden-compartment.jpg
At first glance, you can't tell where Professor Dumpster keeps any of his clothes, bedding, or other important supplies. Then he opens a lid, revealing several hidden compartments under the floor.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/2bfe74b4-3511-45dc-a498-2a456cfc5241/thumbnail/770x578/5f0f1fca2e2702261962ea6fe2068f65/garden.jpg
One element of the Dumpster Project is to grow a sustainable garden alongside the dumpster. Tended by Professor Dumpster and his students, the garden is turning out several kinds of vegetables.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/0509582d-b25b-42c8-b5e8-c0c6f6fc2f6f/thumbnail/770x578/de34dcf3eae8f32fffebd1c7cada4fc0/dumpster-axon-2.png
As a way of demonstrating how much less energy and water he can live on than is used by the average American household, Professor Dumpster plans on installing a set of the average collection of household appliances next to the dumpster that he will use for a few months to establish an energy/water/waste consumption baseline. Then he will be able to compare his own usage to that of the baseline.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/8a8c53fe-bf32-4b6d-b34e-4909ecfbd1e6/thumbnail/770x578/950ca7fc63e539e13bacd44b1997c9db/its-bigger-on-the-inside.jpg
As an homage to Dr. Who and the Tardis, Professor Dumpster has a welcome mat outside the dumpster that reads "It's bigger on the inside."
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/ac469707-3daa-4de5-8f3e-56af8bcd3e0e/thumbnail/770x578/d7f12121ec4b1aaa62228f4230f77259/couchsurfing-note.jpg
Professor Dumpster has not been the only one to live in the dumpster. Because it is a demonstration project, many others -- including his students -- have spent nights there. But he also opened up the dumpster to users of Couchsurfing.com, prompting this note from the first person to ever use that Web-based service to find a bed in a dumpster.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/90f650e0-abeb-425d-90b1-73b439541cb3/thumbnail/770x578/c8f3fb5f035f28af086bbcc5777704da/laying-out-bedpad.jpg
Because the dumpster's interior space is so small, Professor Dumpster must keep his bedding hidden away until he needs it. Here, he begins to set up the bed, first laying out his sleeping pad.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/eb2435a0-ed38-4a7a-a1b6-f09ae132f8c7/thumbnail/770x578/35d587b59ce43c7ec228ea1723fda6d2/star-wars-sheets.jpg
Befitting a geek like Professor Dumpster, he makes his bed using "original" "Star Wars" sheets.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/02725d24-d665-4263-82ee-f77b70fc06e5/thumbnail/770x578/1f90df0309fe2ae0cdde8797a1b2d1a2/mosquito-net.jpg
To attach a mosquito net, Professor Dumpster uses magnets that attach to the metal walls of the dumpster. He also uses magnets to attach many other things to the walls, including drawings by his daughter and other children.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/a775603e-03b0-48c5-b867-942bb2b75fd8/thumbnail/770x578/aab9e90b6f1cdb41c6f66e0c365bce5e/climbing-in.jpg
Professor Dumpster climbs inside his home.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/4f4546af-6301-4ae6-bc9d-b168733f3658/thumbnail/770x578/5a175c9982e08fb9c6be3a2100f832f1/looking-in-top.jpg
The top of the dumpster opens and closes, and when it rains, Professor Dumpster closes it. Here, he looks in on his small home from above.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/8ba9133f-2d96-43ca-b873-90351d09b2b8/thumbnail/770x578/c982a9e75240ef34ae44ce00aaee5531/making-coffee-on-the-patio.jpg
Professor Dumpster calls himself a cross between Bill Nye the Science Guy and Oscar the Grouch.&nbsp; Here, he makes a cup of Turkish Coffee on the bench outside the dumpster while wearing his Oscar the Grouch cap.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/b82b2d3e-fe55-448d-90a8-a8dda0b6f39a/thumbnail/770x578/de376e6cc190b937d4199451605d4619/on-the-trike.jpg
When he needs to get around, he tries to use pedal power -- meaning he rides this three-wheeled bike as much as he can.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/5c76ab5b-d67c-4d8e-bfe3-9279f186e784/thumbnail/770x578/e6040080706564cf70bfcb911f82ca60/prof-dumpster-and-dumpster-cactus.jpg
Professor Dumpster looks over at a cactus sculpture made from the recycled metal of former dumpsters.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/125bbf43-07aa-438b-b5a3-3db9f88b9447/thumbnail/770x578/6505a329257ec843146b2b2583a8405a/mailbox.jpg
This mailbox on the outside of the&nbsp; dumpster is one sign someone lives inside.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/06/30/32556d4b-b854-48ea-8256-1f4eefacc181/thumbnail/770x578/8d0bed2058605eb7a89bef84fbbfccc8/timeline.jpg
The official timeline of the Dumpster Project. On Monday, the project canceled its Kickstarter due to insufficient funding. They had been seeking $100,000, but received less than $16,000.The project is planned out well into next year, including a wide range of expansion and educational initiatives. Professor Dumpster is now hoping people will donate funds directly through its Web site.
 
 
 
 
 
[Date]2014-07-03     Into the wild blue yonder: US Air Force basic training 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e3ca32a0-bfac-4739-ab66-dd597099bd0f/thumbnail/770x578/c3662a21878416dd82bee52227cd9b85/new-trainees-putting-on-new-shoes.jpg
Survive training
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/47822496-1621-485b-ae5c-c3c58c05d738/thumbnail/770x578/201982820c21c94c4122539cd46e826f/graduation-girlfriends-congratulates.jpg
After eight weeks of basic training, the trainees become airmen, and their graduation is celebrated by a large contingent of family and friends. Here, a new airman gets a warm welcome from a friend.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/f34a29a3-167d-4157-8fe1-2f93c89091db/thumbnail/770x578/12814490a6307d9747b175e04c0576f1/new-trainees-line-up-first-thing.jpg
New trainees are broken up into squadrons, and then into groups, known as "flights." Here, a flight of fresh trainees waits outside to be brought in, have their heads shaved, and get all their new gear.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/84bb626f-3bb6-4664-90ee-dc88ef4de22a/thumbnail/770x578/73393d6672a59ae43b546574be198404/new-trainees-ready-to-go-in.jpg
A flight lines up outside the building where they will get their heads shaved and be given their gear. Though they've barely begun their training, they're already required to stand at attention, be silent, and look straight ahead.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/b31891d4-28cf-4917-b2ed-1cf52a420567/thumbnail/770x578/5c43c1707584b5de310d76391fe374e6/new-trainees-with-duffels.jpg
Preparing to go inside the building, the new trainees hold their brand-new duffel bags, which will soon be filled with 40 to 45 pounds of gear.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/9f39e11d-5544-4d81-9894-872ad81fb2cb/thumbnail/770x578/73203736485ad78a81422f9d99fe524c/new-trainee-full-hair.jpg
They may come in with short hair or long hair, but if they're male, it's got to go. Here, a new trainee prepares to say goodbye to his full head of hair.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/2842e78f-ddd4-4b1c-8a7b-d361567c37ac/thumbnail/770x578/b2a1f05ab8213452c583baafae115715/new-trainee-shaved-head.jpg
It took less than two minutes for this trainee, seen in the previous photo with a full head of hair, to have his head shaved. Now he's ready to begin his Air Force training.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/93e75a62-7f32-4459-bfcd-8ecac1d65be5/thumbnail/770x578/ee0097d532d17f4e77b4b48576f3fccb/new-trainee-head-shaving.jpg
For 53 years, Lester West has shaved incoming male trainees' heads. Over that time, he said, he's probably shaved more than a million heads.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/762bb7d6-398e-411d-89df-a43694df51f9/thumbnail/770x578/92fb09db8c30e68645fee654862b3b2d/new-trainee-body-scan-stepping-in.jpg
The Air Force is using a body scanner to determine each trainee's measurements. Here, a trainee is seen stepping into the body scanner.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/d5afea3e-0128-4821-b7db-4f81747c21b5/thumbnail/770x578/0d58fe4bb68b75cd888faa0d4104a3f5/new-trainee-body-scan-standing-still.jpg
A trainee stands still as the body scanner determines his measurements.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/fbeeb782-5640-480e-ac1c-eefd1cb5e14b/thumbnail/770x578/3ee68dc7d40f16d6e78278acdc2f4dc1/new-trainee-going-through-rfid-scanner.jpg
Each and every piece of gear the trainees are given has an embedded RFID tag. When they have suited up and have everything else in their duffel or in their hands, they walk through this scanner, which is meant to determine if they have everything they need.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/8757eda8-a85d-4f8e-a78a-7e1915e702b2/thumbnail/770x578/ce5ea49bc65277feffc0091bffcdf60e/new-trainee-ready-to-check-out.jpg
A brand-new trainee, boots in hand and hat on head, prepares to check out. His eight-week journey to becoming an Air Force airman has begun.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/b5888733-ad22-4374-9e2a-2f8085b4a294/thumbnail/770x578/9e3bbdf0891a536ce10b2e9fd135a959/following-rules.jpg
These rules are posted on the wall for trainees to read and follow as they wait for processing. It's clear, from the last rule in the list, that this sign has been posted since a sexual harassment/assault scandal rocked the Air Force a few years ago. Many of the new procedures in place at Lackland have been instituted in response to the scandal, in which dozens of female trainees said they were sexually assaulted by instructors.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e7d18d61-3604-4be1-b1b5-316a0fb752d2/thumbnail/770x578/f1143c1a824eb88df542b818c48305d5/training-beds-and-lockers.jpg
In a brand-new dormitory building, trainees' beds and lockers are perfectly made and organized during the day while they go through training exercises.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/fc5a18f2-e0fa-405a-8d1b-736e6f6a3ef2/thumbnail/770x578/bbc49895b2971f8303fc95e772622726/training-rifles.jpg
Trainees learn to work with these rifles, which cannot fire live rounds, but which will be used in all weapon drills during their time at Lackland.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/5ce8b47f-98b2-4e44-bd3f-5b606ba7313a/thumbnail/770x578/b75a5c1c335bcbda843414f92bc796b5/training-firing-positions.jpg
Trainees do a wide range of drills during their time at Lackland Air Force Base, including learning how to work from a firing position like this one. Unfortunately, no live training was going on when CNET Road Trip visited.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/7f1b7c1a-7b03-473b-bd85-b1f314f34264/thumbnail/770x578/6c934e92f354277cb465a06d7bae7333/training-computers.jpg
Trainees spend several hours every day in classrooms, learning the academic portion of their Air Force education. Classrooms are filled with non-networked computers. They are not allowed normal outside contact during their eight weeks of training, though they are allowed a few short phone calls to friends or family. They may not access any kind of social media during the training period.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/62ef442e-8828-4ace-a641-44253d5fe743/thumbnail/770x578/68da511cdd53d7845723945598d5fba2/training-tracks.jpg
The trainees go through regular physical exercise, including running around a large track near their barracks. Based on the speed of previous runs, they are categorized into groups, each of which has a specific color. The slowest runners use the red lane, while the fastest use the blue lane. This is meant to apply peer pressure to get better as they proceed through training.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/f9805d1c-c7c1-49cc-ae3c-254c0bbdee91/thumbnail/770x578/34f982693f50c5adbda88c41319b2f02/here-they-come.jpg
After eight weeks, the trainees graduate. But a day before the formal graduation ceremony, they take part in what is known as the "airman's run," where each of the flights dresses in special shirts and runs over this bridge and through a gantlet of their friends and family members.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/3bda4ee3-cbce-40e2-b290-9258bfd7e519/thumbnail/770x578/cf5032a76c8d9ec1b3022e351b903542/airmens-run.jpg
Carrying a group of flags, graduating airmen continue the Airman's run.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/ab19fd27-a343-4b51-9be4-5ae353bd9566/thumbnail/770x578/3bd71e0eb1eb3bd1cdcb64fe2dfd46da/airmens-run-flight-running-in-red.jpg
A group of soon-to-be graduates dressed in the red t-shirts of their flight makes their way through the Airman's run.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/22aec646-3789-4baf-af87-7c65d750d7c5/thumbnail/770x578/4d1939ffab730bd443d7393a401ad891/family-with-sign.jpg
Friends and family line a street at Lackland Air Force base for the Airman's run. Many hold signs that celebrate their loved ones' achievement.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/1c387eb9-a496-4585-b0d8-0e69bd2727a2/thumbnail/770x578/1c954a3092569297e81c02312ff442a1/airmens-run-through-the-crowd.jpg
The soon-to-be graduates make their way through the crowd.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e5b80653-16f7-4758-b7bc-09f6557e24a5/thumbnail/770x578/f59c51775a3ef65e7c97c35e166c21c4/airmens-run-family-with-sign.jpg
Two flights pass by lined up family and friends, some of whom carry signs celebrating the soon-to-be graduates.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/7c16d878-be2b-4406-9278-0663e1b94030/thumbnail/770x578/b292c6fec09db5691b5927bc32be128c/arrving-for-coin-ceremony.jpg
The day before they officially graduate, the new airmen go through what is known as the Coin Ceremony, where they are given the ceremonial coin that signifies their entrance into the Air Force. Here, a flight arrives at the ceremony as hundreds of friends and family, as well as the airmen's instructors look on.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/2ece3b30-5549-469e-96f3-4b218836d5d5/thumbnail/770x578/0f25753667b46e174922f12e04e3de84/edmondson-congratulating-top-airman.jpg
Col. Michele Edmondson, the commander of Air Force basic training, congratulates the top airman, as measured by a wide range of criteria, during the coin ceremony.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/7f7f638d-d9a5-4c08-b398-49ef92346798/thumbnail/770x578/d1692633859ae034c7ebfe261f2c2661/tray-of-coins.jpg
A tray of coins, each of which will be given to a graduating airman. They will likely hold on to those coins for the rest of their Air Force career.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/4c24e9de-c302-4f3c-b1ad-e49ff124b317/thumbnail/770x578/bf97b0fd35cf79c30c6d705194fc5e55/mti-giving-coin.jpg
An instructor hands out a coin to a graduating airman.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/d110af3b-8429-4ce6-b28c-21443f2c2e70/thumbnail/770x578/cd5c686f41cd696532bfeaca7085dcd4/big-hug.jpg
After the Coin Ceremony, friends and family get their first chance to hug their graduating loved one since training began eight weeks earlier.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/1273f9b6-3c38-4876-b22c-69173ce58c02/thumbnail/770x578/953b63a6addc63751bcd2325a9b872fb/graduation-instructors-marching.jpg
A group of military training instructors march at the official graduation ceremony the next day.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e5283a18-91f2-4053-abdc-f01ccfea5978/thumbnail/770x578/7121eeda4a41cd614de68263f5ebc653/graduation-flight-marching.jpg
Each flight marches around the ceremony grounds, in front of their friends and family, as well as gathered instructors, Air Force commanders, and other dignitaries.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/3b14e26e-9cfd-4611-bb93-2989ff2c513e/thumbnail/770x578/2158bfd59f56ed3fb7b01827d3eab7ac/graduation-marching-with-flags.jpg
Airmen carrying the flags of the United States, the Air Force, and each of the states represented by graduating airmen march on graduation day.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/66d4da7a-1af8-40b2-b073-58a51cddc8f0/thumbnail/770x578/50e8a7565e59969b8d23657d1198adeb/graduation-oath.jpg
The graduates take their official oath to the Air Force.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/fd849c5f-7363-482f-ac6b-fc5146ed0ab7/thumbnail/770x578/a368ddb70fe9ac202027f2aaeaa7a18d/next-gen-of-trainees.jpg
Master Sgt. David Drennon, who leads all the basic training instructors, with his two daughters. The son of an Air Force family himself, could he have fathered the next generation of Air Force airmen?

[Date]2014-07-06
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e816d904-baaa-46ef-8a32-f69b6d07978e/thumbnail/770x578/c961ebaa066ed49e9232139cb4d08623/uw-iss.jpg
NASA Training

Most weekdays, NASA puts two of its astronauts through training sessions at the NBL, where they'll spend six hours underwater, each working with rotating teams of safety-, camera-, and support-divers.Before the astronauts come out to suit up, though, support teams lay out their suits in preparation.

In a control room above the NBL pool, technicians monitor up to 21 different camera views of the astronauts' work on the ISS mock-up from in and around the pool.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/e645ae18-5d34-4563-843f-3221766eec5f/thumbnail/770x578/a9adcb42782e1a6ec8f7f6843df908af/kelly-gloves-helmet-laid-out.jpg
Mark and Scott Kelly are part of a NASA experiment to see how space affects both members of a set of twins.When CNET visited, Scott Kelly was slated to be working in the NBL pool. Here, his gloves and helmet are seen laid out and awaiting his arrival to suit up.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/70af89a0-069a-4a72-90a2-7b003574b287/thumbnail/770x578/adcb101715ab00240187db2d78e0b4d8/orion.jpg
A mock-up of NASA's Orion capsule -- which is the space agency's next manned aircraft -- at the NBL.

Inside the main space suit, the astronauts wear a thinner outfit that has integrated components for connecting with the systems built into the space suit.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/42b5a1df-0114-48cc-8b6e-c2aaf7caa924/thumbnail/770x578/ca8cb95beec3148ed329c33d1b9b6931/uw-trainer.jpg
Part of the ISS mock-up, seen under the water at the NBL.

Inside his space suit, Scott Kelly had a Camelbak from which he could drink water. The mouthpiece is seen here sticking up from inside prior to his putting the suit on.

NBL technicians help Scott Kelly stand up after he's begun to put on the space suit pants.

With the help of a couple of NBL technicians, Kelly climbs up into the main part of the space suit.

Astronaut Scott Kelly, who along with his brother Mark Kelly, is part of a team that will help NASA study the effects of space on both members of a set of twins.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/02/3f3be63e-6ca7-4735-803a-851cbc63d411/thumbnail/770x578/6873bda62974b44a457059c7e956ab6d/moment-of-rest.jpg
After getting into the space suit, Scott Kelly rests for a moment before putting on his helmet.

[Date]2014-07-09      Rockin' with Elvis at Graceland
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/0428160a-b245-4ad4-a893-384163740ad3/thumbnail/770x578/fe7d8e54d49248f34ffe02d9c20039e9/suits-and-records-in-racquetball-court.jpg
Elvis home
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/cf9c890f-7eb4-43cf-b796-ea4c107e43f0/thumbnail/770x578/3de7a40dd5921e0fa39c7e96bf1aa94d/front-of-house.jpg
If you've never been to Graceland, you might think that Elvis' famous mansion is huge.But while it's by no means a small house, it's also manageable and stately. Seen here is the front of the mansion.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/46ab7496-53c9-4a4e-83a7-5c6a04ca121c/thumbnail/770x578/ee9d06cc4d25749dd2695062c6973637/music-room.jpg
A look into Elvis' living room, near the front entrance of Graceland. Elvis would hold court in the room and play music on the piano in the far room in the rear of the picture.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/829e5554-e132-4f31-85fc-6567150aa036/thumbnail/770x578/1f0c551286e5693f0d13d1d62fb908ed/kitchen-1.jpg
Nothing special by today's standards, the Graceland kitchen was surely luxurious when Elvis moved into the 1939 house in 1957.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/191235a8-e354-48e8-b68d-070931c3b4ce/thumbnail/770x578/82c28ab573e0f3a51697fc2376de8207/kitchen-2.jpg
A look at the other side of the Graceland kitchen.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/5dae99f5-8dab-4227-a2aa-17a13d5169a1/thumbnail/770x578/3f818f6671524f3cd450e7a81bb26b98/e250-at-graceland.jpg
The Mercedes-Benz E250 Bluetec that CNET reporter Daniel Terdiman has been road-testing on Road Trip 2014, seen parked just outside the main gates to Graceland.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/84ed45a8-c0bc-491e-8127-60c07c98ab12/thumbnail/770x578/02567061cd960ef9e23c3f9f3301e599/tv-lounge.jpg
Elvis' TV lounge, where the rock and roll star liked to watch TV with friends.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/4dcc143d-5368-4962-8625-97e9bf123876/thumbnail/770x578/59d74c9911f3573471a82562fa9a0519/tv-lounge-bar.jpg
What TV lounge would be complete without a matching bar?
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/6b7a9df2-f52c-41e1-8f8f-690c3ec2f347/thumbnail/770x578/5306fab7adb6a4e62a0c30b886b2be28/billiards-room.jpg
Graceland features many different design motifs, with no consistent style from room to room. This is the billiards room, which has a style unlike anything else in the famous mansion. Elvis decorated the room himself in 1974, according to Threads, and he used more than 300 yards of fabric to do so.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/e41bb03d-acf0-48f5-9d3e-38f8218128f2/thumbnail/770x578/de636faf60a4aacc3b3f3d565ba10966/jungle-room.jpg
Elvis' famous jungle room. According to Elvis.com, "the Jungle Room has become famous over the years due to the eccentric design with a Polynesian influence, reminiscent of Elvis' favorite vacation spot -- Hawaii. The detailed wooden carvings in the furniture and the green shag carpet of the 1970s makes this an Elvis fan favorite."
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/b3879536-edc1-4a3a-b71a-262703f1b921/thumbnail/770x578/2a6fd452ab9756aa4bd0a8f62ac29198/lisa-marie-swing-set.jpg
Behind the main house on the 13.8-acre Graceland estate is this small cottage, where Elvis' father, Vernon Presley, managed the star's business affairs. Placed in front of the cottage is this swing set, which Elvis bought for his daughter, Lisa Marie, in the 1970s.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/de372833-fece-457c-807a-e90a33ae5928/thumbnail/770x578/43f00a430e24c438c388d3e0c0fa9ab4/hall-of-gold.jpg
Elvis had more than 150 hit records during his career, many of which earned him gold and platinum records from RCA, his label, and the Recording Industry Association of America.Many of those gold and platinum records, along with plenty of other memorabilia from his career, is housed in this room, known as the Hall of Gold.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/e3c29e44-9d18-4267-a71c-7d401ab31849/thumbnail/770x578/49cad7efea881a9fc59ad8c0e2257f51/dont-be-cruel-five-gold-records.jpg
This is a commemoration of Elvis' song "Don't Be Cruel" having sold five million copies.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/f2479def-5619-4fb3-8ee9-d01d7c5a85e3/thumbnail/770x578/2371c6d658548c2855c0e52ff4c90157/so-many-gold-records.jpg
A walk down through the Hall of Gold makes you realize just how successful an entertainer Elvis was, at least as measured by awards and sales.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/d6080609-1958-4fee-9a5a-766dfe035af5/thumbnail/770x578/910899fb10cf5ce46cd69b991d2fb2b4/hall-of-gold-records-on-wall.jpg
Another look at the nearly endless collection of gold and platinum records Elvis earned in his short career. He died at Graceland when he was only 42.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/205c3a15-754d-443d-bbd7-f4852b34016c/thumbnail/770x578/55421f1baa0f5b603acd411c2926fd11/elvis-suits.jpg
In addition to housing many of his gold and platinum records and other awards and commemorations, the former racquetball court also houses a number of the outlandish suits Elvis wore when he performed in Las Vegas.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/8a9a6f2b-f07d-4b5c-a6ff-f5c2790a11f8/thumbnail/770x578/be973b7453c324af37d20ea87067353c/meditation-garden.jpg
Graceland visitors' last tour stop is the Meditation Garden, which is a place to pause and quietly contemplate the life of one of the biggest stars in American history. Elvis, along with his parents, his grandmother, and his twin brother -- who died at birth -- are all buried here.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/d5690144-a7e8-44f3-b938-920a3513abaf/thumbnail/770x578/80392d2ccbf694c283d7f1e07810b4ba/rolls-royces.jpg
Many Graceland visitors also check out the associated museum housing many of Elvis' cars and other vehicles.These are two Rolls-Royce Silver Clouds. The white one is a 1966 model, which he eventually traded in.The black one is a 1960 Silver Cloud, which was Elvis' first Rolls, though he owned several during his life.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/a678b147-bcc9-4999-adbb-5f01f4a2f053/thumbnail/770x578/ddd852425c80e2f47a9d7688c54213ca/ferrari.jpg
This is a 1975 Ferrari Dino, which Elvis bought used in 1976 for $20,583.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/c7368053-dff4-470f-b94e-be2fa7a0e411/thumbnail/770x578/9875b4a8fa931d2cf2fad45057790c33/lincoln-continental.jpg
This is Elvis' 1956 Lincoln Continental Mark II. It was a rare car that cost $10,000 when new, far more than the $4,000 average price of a Cadillac. According to Graceland, Elvis bought this Lincoln after his first one was covered in lipstick graffiti left by fans.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/ade06500-b90c-4c24-ba91-44219f37c618/thumbnail/770x578/391f2a652cad96cbc908443a735797b0/stutz.jpg
Elvis was driving this 1973 Stutz Blackhawk, one of his favorite cars, when he drove through the gates of Graceland for the final time, on August 16, 1977.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/20124ed3-2597-49ac-94c9-257d69d9f1a5/thumbnail/770x578/b3112b2ec64269552c003fb8d635e631/pink-cadillac.jpg
According to Graceland, this may be the most famous of Elvis' cars, a pink 1955 Cadillac Fleetwood. He first used it to tour, but then gave it to his mother, who loved it. It became known as "Gladys' car."
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/265413b5-6c94-4e4e-a88a-0ab51e8bf3e3/thumbnail/770x578/990a49c995622beb9d41c8c8fac8c3dc/limo.jpg
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/265413b5-6c94-4e4e-a88a-0ab51e8bf3e3/thumbnail/770x578/990a49c995622beb9d41c8c8fac8c3dc/limo.jpg
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/a1edd995-0bc1-49c0-b523-57a2661b665f/thumbnail/770x578/dda0735c58290fe4336f0471e584292d/lisa-marie-airplane.jpg
Originally flown by Delta Airlines, this was a 96-seater Convair 880 built in 1956. Elvis purchased it in 1975 for $250,000, and he spent an additional $800,000 customizing it.Elvis flew on the plane 221 times and named it Lisa Marie, after his daughter.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/695f345a-9bcb-41d7-b16b-97538824be87/thumbnail/770x578/e1c4f5ca255518bb146df1bad4bdd128/on-the-plane-1.jpg
The interior of the Lisa Marie was outfitted with comfortable couches and all the luxuries that Elvis and his many friends could want as they flew around the country.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/5c42c612-4a59-4861-a6e4-1de9d3c1b76c/thumbnail/770x578/378eb8c3fc42bd7dde88ca58aa2cae83/plane-dining-table.jpg
The plane even had a luxurious dining table for six.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/ddf54f04-5ae0-4ec9-b870-43fdbaeeff8b/thumbnail/770x578/a9c9d3c770fa6e6c28733aedd7641e15/plane-elvis-bedroom.jpg
In the rear of the airplane was Elvis' private bedroom suite, complete with queen-size bed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/08/16e3bf0b-ad20-4377-badf-a158ce5d3bb3/thumbnail/770x578/b6b915dd064313a3fdd2188bb2576ec0/jetstar.jpg
Elvis' other airplane was this 10-seater Lockheed JetStar, built in 1960. He purchased it in 1975 for just under $900,000 and nicknamed it the "Hound Dog II."Elvis' support staff used the plane to fly ahead when he was on tour, to make sure all the arrangements were in order for his arrival.
 
 
 
 
 
[Date]2014-07-11    Why FedEx beats up packages in a lab 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/63d867ac-950c-43eb-8c1d-c33574382a67/thumbnail/770x578/eacf21a541d49bd842ab01b4a96bbcfd/compression-machine-in-action.jpg
Here, we see an engineer inspecting how a package is performing while being compressed with more than 50 pounds of pressure.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/f1b5eed2-b50d-4666-9c81-3dfb519bb5eb/thumbnail/770x578/1e82d8923c87cc413a431efc5d257a77/drop-machine-1.jpg
A technician prepares to drop a package using a machine that lifts it up and then slams it down to the floor. The idea is to test each and every side and edge of the package. Boxes aimed at the domestic market will be dropped 10 times, while those that go international will hit the ground 20 times.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/e9e8963f-9e07-44a0-be27-86a5d91dc494/thumbnail/770x578/63159cb70e1fd6017bebdefbc5afa8d4/drop-machine-2.jpg
A package falls rapidly after the machine slammed it to the floor.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/6e562a19-07b8-4777-a61e-f97977c42b65/thumbnail/770x578/65155eee38dbb4b7dd268728659d634d/vibration-machine.jpg
This is the Package Lab's vibration machine. Packages are put on this machine and vibrated to mimic what they'll go through on a FedEx truck or airplane.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/b55e98a7-e70d-4bf1-af15-8e31c31d9aad/thumbnail/770x578/a1c2d4b972a9a2c1ed122ba065be6dd8/compression-machine.jpg
In order to test how strong a package is, the lab puts them into this compression machine, which applies significant pressure. If the box buckles before too much pressure is applied, it's clear that it will not withstand being stacked under many other boxes.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/52d19840-5d21-4287-9c21-ebde5ab93c0a/thumbnail/770x578/6163daf9875fe8533212f0ce7ce5ca78/freight-machine.jpg
Large freight packages are put on this sled and then slammed backward to mimic the beating they'll take either on a truck or plane, or when someone is carrying them around on a forklift.
 
Large freight packages are put on this sled and then slammed backward to mimic the beating they'll take either on a truck or plane, or when someone is carrying them around on a forklift.
A look at the freight sled in action.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/9b344ba8-3ebc-4502-8621-cd10c4d0b839/thumbnail/770x578/05e6d35d30c1d4f819e86e0932457d32/altitude-machine.jpg
This machine lets lab engineers test how a package or its contents will perform at high altitudes. The idea is to see if it can perform satisfactorily when being driven, say, over the Rocky Mountains.
 
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/181c13fd-da64-4003-99e0-962baabb5edb/thumbnail/770x578/1876d5cfdc338351714903a64632597a/temperature-machine.jpg
This machine can subject a package to hot or cold temperatures, in order to be sure it, or its contents, can survive those extremes.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/10/7c02d925-dda3-426a-8422-a97b15818878/thumbnail/770x578/2be666b94ca887006b303e79389f8ee1/cubesat-shot.jpg
FedEx has begun shipping CubeSats, or small satellites, and helped some of its clients by designing a custom package for the devices.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/9dbb6fa0-8f50-48bc-b7d7-48ab4d6a2c41/thumbnail/770x578/9b4c4353c2d4dd659a9b07fcf98d3e5f/guitars.jpg
Another service offered by the Package Lab is package design.
Customers who want to find a new way to box up various products can ask
the lab to help them customize a solution. An example is these three guitars, which are similar but subtly different. The manufacturer wanted to find a single package that could hold any one of them, rather than having to rely on a different type of box for each.&nbsp; The idea is to allow the company to save money by being able to buy boxes at scale. FedEx came up with a way to achieve the goal.
 
 
[Date]2014-07-12    
At FedEx's Memphis hub, sorting 1.5 million packages
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/b3bd2014-9d1d-44c0-bf5b-3b37b2162746/thumbnail/770x578/dacd672e1f6acaa62f5274348fef471a/md-11.jpg
Every night, FedEx sends 140 planes to Memphis, and then sends 140 planes back out. Every one of the 1.5 million packages that comes through the World Hub will be sent back out toward its final destination.FedEx operates numerous types of planes, including this McDonnell Douglas MD-11. It also flies Boeing 777s, 767s, and 757s; Airbus 300s and 310s; and McDonnell Douglas MD-10s.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/53f55855-1ad8-442d-9bfa-1649281bd68e/thumbnail/770x578/af4b5e930cf0c165d64d557f60c13bb5/unloading-md-11.jpg
A FedEx crew works feverishly in the rain to unload thousands of packages from an MD-11.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/57bad6f1-d963-4371-b597-2d1cd9498845/thumbnail/770x578/22ebc27d95d8ad18fc5c53047ecdbfc5/containers-outside-plane.jpg
Workers check out containers full of thousands of packages that have just been unloaded from a FedEx MD-11 at its Memphis World Hub.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/06bf012a-c190-4c13-a3f4-c1cd56334765/thumbnail/770x578/d200955d8389b8972d414eb04cf2ed8b/hubinput.jpg
After packages are unloaded from planes at FedEx's Memphis World Hub, they're brought to one of nine Input areas: five for domestic packages and four that handle international, heavyweight, and dangerous-goods packages.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/0745a86f-b209-482c-b561-8472d0e4da1c/thumbnail/770x578/8a4e60469e95b7d5fcb61faf300eaa74/flooding-the-matrix.jpg
One container's worth of packages -- about 235 -- floods into the Matrix. From there, FedEx workers take them and send them out on conveyors, where they're scanned and sorted for placement on planes that will take them to their final destination.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/49bef5e3-6466-49f7-8923-ecc253cc9af8/thumbnail/770x578/a65a6fbb53610de6b19b035be84ea952/matrix.jpg
Workers at the Matrix process thousands of packages an hour.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/bf6630ba-bdbb-4ae5-a4cb-b66f6e9adecb/thumbnail/770x578/471579efb6c926eac9a87108ed030158/packages-going-through-scanner.jpg
After going through the Matrix, packages pass through a scanner, which reads their label -- complete with a bar code -- and sends them on their way to be sorted onto the plane that will take them to their eventual destination.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/11/7af08a84-8bb0-4d30-a9f6-cfe877ac6be9/thumbnail/770x578/36bd8b6577da850d9cabca8f4a95e593/looking-down-at-belts.jpg
A look down at row after row of conveyor belts moving packages through FedEx's World Hub in Memphis, Tenn.

A package is pushed off a conveyor belt at a diverter, which sends the parcel on its way toward its eventual destination.

At the SPSS, workers sort packages onto one of three belts. The packages are eventually sorted into bags that are designated for specific geographic destinations.

Inside Frank Lloyd Wright's only skyscraper
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/289bf498-643e-48e2-bc58-3949e868b5a8/thumbnail/770x578/1c8a5cbb184532731a8e7f5aade1f73f/pt-from-the-west-aerial.jpg
A look at Price Tower from the west, as photographed by a DJI Phantom 2 Vision + quadcopter. The 19-story building is visible from nearly everywhere in Bartlesville.Today, the building is managed by the Price Tower Arts Center, a nonprofit. However, there are also a hotel, a bar, and some private offices still in use in the building.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/754606a5-d9c4-43f0-9017-5d30c9cf9a3e/thumbnail/770x578/550e3c69f3a912bc6277e4b3516b949b/louvers-with-owl.jpg
Though the Price Tower has louvers on all sides, these are the only ones that are meant to be moved intentionally. Found on the veranda outside what was originally the Price Company's corporate apartment, they are topped with a fake owl that scares off birds.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/5caed431-7862-4fef-a1ca-57409c8d6635/thumbnail/770x578/ca57a261beedb7837f5f2d9d2ed70ac0/corporate-apartment-1.jpg
For Wright, a skyscraper meant a building that was used in many different ways. So the Price Tower contained apartments, offices, and retail space. This is the Price Company's corporate apartment, which was used by the company's VIP guests, or its employees when they were in Bartlesville. It has been maintained to look much like it did when the Price Company was still using the building.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/50046355-b783-4a21-bca0-93c1c4b74968/thumbnail/770x578/2ca50d92261d0be0cddfb04f46f4423f/corporate-apartment-flw-mural.jpg
Another look at the corporate apartment, including an abstract mural Wright had painted on the wall of the apartment.

In the bottom right corner of the mural in the corporate apartment, Wright left this inscription to Hal Price: "The Blue Moon - To Hal. Frank Lloyd Wright." This was a reference to Wright's feeling that his collaboration with Price was so good as to be as rare as a blue moon.

The corporate apartment, including the Frank Lloyd Wright mural and exact replicas of original Frank Lloyd Wright-designed drapes.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/912616c7-4aee-4d49-ac07-d4d25f826ef6/thumbnail/770x578/596efd355c2239067fd6de0b9731f6f9/pt-from-the-east-aerial.jpg
An aerial view of Price Tower from the east, shot using a DJI Phantom 2 Vision + quadcopter.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/5ff2bc2b-33e4-44ee-af75-5c7a90bcd155/thumbnail/770x578/a86cfbbcfc6d6aa5a7c5c76830ca9b05/corporate-apartment-built-in-table.jpg
Wright enjoyed putting built-in furniture in his buildings because it gave him more control over how people would use them. An example is this built-in table in the Price Tower corporate apartment.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/a6dbff97-478a-4226-9c19-883d8796f6ee/thumbnail/770x578/e644d075e199d8fe9a88a7a0998220ea/photo-14.jpg
A look at Price Tower from ground level on the south side of the building.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/45653341-ce48-47d7-80a1-6895d84be987/thumbnail/770x578/4c026002b5bbef85a932462096774ec8/corporate-apartment-kitchen.jpg
The kitchen in the corporate apartment was suitably small, but it did the job, and included all the important appliances. Underneath the stove are both the oven and the refrigerator.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/1b231636-ccb0-410f-8686-4c970eec0766/thumbnail/770x578/e8252414122be507737decba5dd2d0e1/veranda-with-tables.jpg
A patio outside the Copper Bar. Enjoy a drink or some food with terrific views of the Bartlesville area.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/81e9ec07-140d-48d6-a7e3-0bd22b07fb86/thumbnail/770x578/0088c2d7e637d17478f3b65a272ec0aa/pt-showing-pts-veranda.jpg
This aerial view of Price Tower, also shot with a DJI Phantom 2 Vision +, shows the building from the west, and makes it easy to see the huge veranda outside what was Hal Price's private office.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/a502b2f9-20e5-41ea-8e70-20b54d8419b5/thumbnail/770x578/a9910f5a4dd43361aef44dbf9ac35911/spire.jpg
A look at Price Tower's spire, jutting up from the core of the building.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/e090b0a7-0dec-4c32-9e55-9bdb4af1c497/thumbnail/770x578/a72da7ebecaf30df839176ed09711ca2/corporate-apartment-4.jpg
A final look at the corporate apartment, showing the drapes, and several chairs Wright designed.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/17aaabaf-820c-4874-88f7-3dda661fe91f/thumbnail/770x578/0244409d8cfb71a6e806642ec45c438b/water-damage.jpg
Wright's buildings are famous for having leaks, and Price Tower is no exception. This built-in shelf in the corporate apartment was damaged by leaked water.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/834a5341-751a-4622-8851-ab934bdd29aa/thumbnail/770x578/11c5d7e4b410b93f956eea38a643dfa8/pt-from-the-north-aerial.jpg
A view of the Price Tower, as seen from the north side of the building, shot by a DJI Phantom 2 Vision + quadcopter.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/fc33d858-db2e-40f1-b27d-31fffc666da0/thumbnail/770x578/d70cb7290a6ae8e43b4154ebd5a2cb19/boardroom.jpg
When the Price Company was still using the Price Tower, its board consisted of only four members, so its boardroom was this foyer space just outside the elevators on the 18th floor.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/092aaaea-cd3b-4be2-8504-845266b27d4a/thumbnail/770x578/409749f792f491545d0732230f823359/globe.jpg
Almost everywhere you look in and around Price Tower are sharp angles, especially triangles. There are few, if any, circles.When Price and Wright were still in the design stage, Price insisted on a large map of the world for his wall, but Wright hated the idea. Still, as the owner of a global pipeline company, Price needed to have a map of the world in his office so he could consult with clients about the location of their projects. The compromise was this globe. Wright had it placed behind the door.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/2783ec39-0d55-45c1-970a-abf17c4b9057/thumbnail/770x578/b0da3e5d2f4dbc7de78d1d34f6b5a765/hcp-desk-1.jpg
In Price's office, Wright designed a built-in desk that could be used from either side. It has drawers on both sides, a chair on one side, and this bench on the other.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/a51f47a4-ebfc-407a-a055-efe51e5bc93d/thumbnail/770x578/4673c6f82ab4dc6092d6039d199c428d/hcp-desk-with-abstract-mural.jpg
A look at Price's private office, on the 19th floor of the building.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/d34911d9-2e2e-48a0-bc72-7d0ba995f409/thumbnail/770x578/198b422c0a385b5dc2e09f935f889b49/fireplace.jpg
A signature of Wright's buildings, even his skyscraper, is the fireplace. This one is located in Price's private office.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/d498103d-352e-4796-898f-30053d5ef088/thumbnail/770x578/317339f788bf01ca8103282e625c7df7/flw-chairs.jpg
Wright designed these chairs, which were used throughout the Price Company. They were said to be very uncomfortable.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/b32c6ffe-7934-46d6-82e7-00ff2b2390d7/thumbnail/770x578/e770230276cb3ee04309b9a13666166e/flw-desk-chair-hcp-office.jpg
This is the desk chair used by Hal Price in his private office. Wright also designed this chair.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/650098a6-814a-4b18-8b01-74335c878a18/thumbnail/770x578/269fb74ef3d9c1823b5e3d0f6fb3d11f/hanging-desk-lamp.jpg
Wright designed this hanging desk lamp, which utilizes the triangle shape, because he hated the idea of a lamp being placed on the desk.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/d8caa694-acde-4b3e-9950-221d77c2b51b/thumbnail/770x578/26dd93e682de180fa6e98a8d5a6f2ca7/triangles-in-ceiling.jpg
Look at just about any ceiling in Price Tower and you'll find more triangles.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/58a56de2-625d-4fa0-945f-5a0c990471a0/thumbnail/770x578/7e695803fde50b1386474c56f3508ac1/hcp-secretary-desk.jpg
This is Hal Price's secretary's desk, which is located just outside Price's private office on the 19th floor.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/4030c137-1da5-45a7-9177-48813b443d36/thumbnail/770x578/3f53feafd5a108f7d0b0195e8209daff/rug.jpg
Wright designed this large carpet, which was originally installed in a separate house Wright designed for the Price family.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/8f795edf-496e-4755-b39e-16c5cf243435/thumbnail/770x578/2c0505b5d01e88065ab65b19134dac30/hcp-logo.jpg
Wright designed a corporate logo for the Price Company, and every floor of the building has one embedded there. The building is oriented in the same direction as the logo.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/852b2f0b-38d2-454b-81e3-6ecc153608f1/thumbnail/770x578/26f9836b19ed1356fc4c27dbb7a91e08/copper-bar-1.jpg
Though the Copper Bar, located inside the Price Tower, was not designed by Wright, the space was set up by someone trying hard to be faithful to his aesthetic.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/3ab1bc98-c6de-418c-8765-ba6f42b22ef0/thumbnail/770x578/5ff608e191cddcc18ba28a25dbca0b61/copper-bar-3.jpg
A look at the sharp angles and multiple levels of the Copper Bar.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/8fbb1eac-1e3e-4a6c-8df1-d7811e865fcc/thumbnail/770x578/a04d049be57530a70c01f3d5cb41d05c/former-dress-shop.jpg
Today, this is the building's main foyer, but when Price Tower opened, this ground-floor space was a dress shop, helping to meet Wright's requirement that the building be mixed-use.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/18/404140ab-67c3-4bd5-bb40-72f238dc62eb/thumbnail/770x578/62f82bf4f0efb72317bedd07ecbfc27e/pt-phillips-66.jpg
A view of the Price Tower from several blocks away in Bartlesville. In the foreground is a Phillips 66 gas station. Bartlesville is best known as the corporate headquarters of Phillips Petroleum, later Conoco Phillips. And the Phillips company purchased the Price Tower when Price himself decided he didn't need it any more.
 
 
[Date]2014-07-22
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/7a4bf5b7-9973-498a-a2a4-072c1a890792/thumbnail/770x578/ac3ecdec9087497d24d8710eb9b5c437/barrell-begun-winding.jpg
Here you can see what is known as a "barrel," the very beginning of a front section. The barrel is comprised of several smaller sections known as mandrels. Once the mandrels assembled, a giant machine methodically winds thousands of pounds of composite "slit tape" around the barrel, gradually forming the shape of the forward section.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/2d65b037-d3e0-4e7a-85d4-751305ee9421/thumbnail/770x578/b56eeba3289b4995245191591c8e43ce/barrell-begun-winding-different-angle.jpg
Still being wrapped in composite material, the barrel is suspended between two sides of this giant blue tool. Once the wrapping is complete, the barrel will be placed in one of the world's largest autoclaves.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/66c7904a-9f1a-4f84-87a5-c912f3bc4b90/thumbnail/770x578/f9ed849425da74dabe76d76506de9c08/bag-over-barrell.jpg
Before all the different mandrels are put in place, the incomplete barrel is wrapped in this "bag." Once the final mandrel is added, the bag will be removed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/c1a826a3-094b-4551-a8bc-104c277465e5/thumbnail/770x578/30d228280e9003868299450ff2e1f09d/mandrel-with-window-impressions.jpg
A mandrel section already shows where the Dreamliner's windows will be cut out.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/052ea620-0e4e-497c-b84b-fa85470dab78/thumbnail/770x578/40d3b0271a9378bffe8cf947af5097ba/composite-rolls.jpg
Most of Boeing's airplanes have traditionally been made with aluminum. But with the 787 Dreamliner, it began using composite materials. These are rolls of the composite tape that will be wrapped around a barrel.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/b1ddd691-8c70-4d09-8155-866189f1339e/thumbnail/770x578/38b2492cd6c07a5ccef2592d82d1678c/machine-winding-composite.jpg
A giant tool automatically applies the composite tape to the barrel.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/41e93b21-0235-43cc-bb55-e0cdbbe2fe29/thumbnail/770x578/d33f6ef8900d6ff8c69a98f039e2eaa1/autoclave-empty.jpg
When it was built in the mid-2000s, this was the world's largest autoclave. Now, it's just inches shorter than the world's biggest.When the Dreamliner barrels are ready, they are placed in here and "cooked" for about 10 hours. Spirit Aerosystems doesn't reveal the temperature or pressure that the barrels undergo.Just to the left of the autoclave is the door, which is rolled into placed and locked prior to "cooking."
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/7d98bb4c-7cc6-48de-a7cb-2f07c66a876f/thumbnail/770x578/529ab7264b8260144860c9b88a89294f/1204847-004.jpg
In this photo, we see a Dreamliner barrel inside the autoclave -- though the cooking only happens when the door is locked in place.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/5fff93b0-1c70-4ce5-9cb1-68d2a7f1e21c/thumbnail/770x578/2b6d14c3af4b43a068360b3476951365/out-of-autoclave-no-markings.jpg
When a barrel goes into the autoclave, it is black. When it comes out, it is this silver color. That makes it easy to tell if a Dreamliner barrel has been in the autoclave or not. When the barrel comes out, it's also entirely smooth, with nothing cut out.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/85260529-b231-489f-a85d-a8eb2d4ea86c/thumbnail/770x578/b44cdcc79086d474010bc24e35fdcfa0/out-of-autoclave-window-markings.jpg
The next step is to mark the various areas that must be cut out of the barrel, such as the windows and exit doors.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/849e1b5c-e3ac-4569-8fe7-046875f9da97/thumbnail/770x578/659caae272032cf769f7e80652ebc69e/out-of-autoclave-cut-outs.jpg
Next, workers cut out the various windows, doors, and landing gear sections.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/1ce87ce6-0bec-4103-ba1f-cb99c06fe10b/thumbnail/770x578/2026bcdfb251a1a452bcfe8a8b1bbe0b/787-canted-inside-trim-and-drill.jpg
Here, we see a Dreamliner front section canted to one side as it sits in the trim and drill position. The front section can be rotated on its central axis any way that's necessary to allow workers the easiest access.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/dd40ce6d-ee2e-4137-82bd-cbeb1e0fa9cd/thumbnail/770x578/65357f05cb10f831687e57c38081797f/fastening-pieces-to-structure.jpg
A front section is suspended upside down as workers fasten various components to its structure to increase its strength. These components are generally aluminum or titanium and are only installed on the interior of the structure.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/0a9fa72b-3426-4bd4-ad28-a3657651d2e3/thumbnail/770x578/838ce793f4a9161615b100c568ac5026/final-assembly.jpg
In the final assembly area, Spirit works on installing systems in as many as eight Dreamliner front sections at a time, while also having two stations where the Dreamliners are powered-up for the first time.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/324f86b1-c448-4aa3-8c0a-d02fdaf8ab49/thumbnail/770x578/2332dc800201c7d9e5b018106f5204fa/final-assembly-fuselage-empty.jpg
Until reaching final assembly, the Dreamliner front section is largely an empty cylinder.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/b2fefb02-c527-4329-9fd6-37349966c452/thumbnail/770x578/6b1f55a6926c9d9fa8f857eda30c96d9/lined-up-in-final-assembly.jpg
Dreamliner front sections lined up for installation of various systems.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/00f61f5a-8fa5-4e69-8549-dc4b7e1b0589/thumbnail/770x578/0ad046957200979dbae790dce47592f6/cockpit-windows.jpg
A look at the cockpit windows on a Dreamliner front section in final assembly.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/1260adba-a2fc-4cde-9fc3-fdee314a8173/thumbnail/770x578/17487b8ace23e3a3a7acac071a20294d/radome-in-nose.jpg
The nose of this Dreamliner front section is lifted so that workers can install a special radar and antenna package that is used to help the plane navigate and anticipate weather.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/e3660868-4ab4-4665-a0cf-8a6d4d82397e/thumbnail/770x578/90fec8ee7cd120a28bf7669d88d38334/cockpit-much-work-to-do.jpg
The cockpit of a Dreamliner that still needs a wide range of systems installed.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/970bfaff-8765-4610-89e1-0a9fc7d3eba7/thumbnail/770x578/6c1f177181106454209e2cf518cce0f6/cockpit-in-progress.jpg
A wider look at a Dreamliner cockpit in the process of having various systems installed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/5937cd22-0dbc-4eb6-8606-acf1a5ce9293/thumbnail/770x578/fb9229f70bebe78894825583a06266bf/fuselage-mostly-empty.jpg
The fuselage of this Dreamliner front section is still mostly empty, though some systems have been installed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/3fcac29c-c3ec-4f5f-b6ea-b0a5c77acba7/thumbnail/770x578/eb00b15e39d54bb3203c9a2fead8a29b/1401386-010.jpg
Even though this Dreamliner is still just a front section, it is powered up prior to shipping to Boeing. Many of the cockpit systems are tested as if the plane was complete. The aircraft doesn't know that it doesn't have wings or the rest of its body.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/d2e807ff-adae-4f93-ba96-903b16826ee8/thumbnail/770x578/c2241befa4e2939d2ee0a0210912ee8f/1401386-007.jpg
Another look at a powered-up Dreamliner cockpit.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/102bbb90-4080-41fe-a0d5-b43889fc5a36/thumbnail/770x578/553cbc2eb1077283e4e230e96301091f/nose-up.jpg
The nose on this Dreamliner front section is lifted so that workers can install the radar and antenna package.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/d6be5357-cebe-4ebf-a719-59c65b6351f2/thumbnail/770x578/c0da273ab3ddb34c0e04421f2fd003d4/ready-to-ship.jpg
After everything has been done, it's time to send the Dreamliner front sections to Boeing. Here, two of them sit, ready to be loaded onto a Dreamlifter and then flown to Washington state or South Carolina.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/3481c1c4-2990-46f5-9247-8b627e35ca7a/thumbnail/770x578/020a3b273e8f96090d8f6d97aa0414a3/0701960-042.jpg
A completed Dreamliner front section is seen being loaded onto the Dreamlifter, the special airplane Boeing built to fly the Dreamliner's major components to its factories in Washington state or South Carolina for final assembly.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/0e49e26f-d6fb-4a26-a7cc-75c7a0955ca0/thumbnail/770x578/06cae5fe946bc04a422b781fe32f72b2/0701960-078.jpg
A look at the massive Dreamlifter.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/19/170625db-e73b-4d04-a288-c03870091ca5/thumbnail/770x578/d119d95593a7bb02a2ef83274c06ab27/0701960-080.jpg
A Dreamlifter as it takes off on its way to Boeing.
 
 
[Date]2014-07-26
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/b4136484-2f00-4078-af74-5d9538170a2b/thumbnail/770x578/38bf54cdd70348fc224790704801a563/working-inside-cockpit-section.jpg
Here, we see a Spirit technician working inside the all-aluminum front of a 737 cockpit, seen inside Spirit's massive facility here.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/8f1eb829-b406-48b6-9ec4-a66283a70155/thumbnail/770x578/2831ba186e8257e64ee6a30a341a560a/0601238-001.jpg
This is "Integration," where all six major sections of a 737 are fused together into a full fuselage. At Spirit Aerosystems, the spot from which this photo was taken is known as the "scenic overlook."
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/dd3f358a-a44b-49a5-9bee-41f18211f4fc/thumbnail/770x578/4d192389e1c4a9f932ad8eb8cbec013b/0602281-004.jpg
Last month, a train carrying 737 fuselages to Boeing in the Seattle area derailed in Montana, causing three of the fuselages to end up in a river. But normally, the trains make it to Washington safely, looking just like this.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/8d432c7d-a5e4-4f71-89ab-0f40cf264287/thumbnail/770x578/4b651822ee65c4c3f4696a6930bace80/entry-and-galley-panels.jpg
Spirit technicians work on 737 entry and galley panels.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/c6c3f538-7da4-49be-89fd-a308850b1990/thumbnail/770x578/e8a98269c7bc39860099e4207bc73554/trim-and-drill.jpg
Large 737 sections are being worked on inside what are known as "trim and drill," where many of the holes and windows are drilled and cut out of the fuselage.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/db355bc1-70a9-4c4d-b9cb-164327a55426/thumbnail/770x578/2426e26611d306aab7310263c96eec52/forward-sections.jpg
At Spirit Aerosystems in Wichita, technicians work on several 737 forward sections, which include the cockpit area.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/76f51c15-a9d5-45e4-b9d5-cad1472080c9/thumbnail/770x578/4291071a0bde6b46752f1882f57bf47b/underneath-entry-and-galley-panels.jpg
A look at the underside of the unfinished entry and galley panels.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/19950b4d-4be8-4f7b-8d6e-a89be13d417c/thumbnail/770x578/8006db9f3b8df76488805158bf568517/cockpit-sections.jpg
Two 737 cockpit sections sit on the floor at Spirit Aerosystems in Wichita, Kan.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/cea09145-ddeb-4cfa-b742-4d4076abdef7/thumbnail/770x578/730f7395f2d78d8589cd9749517df631/robot-working.jpg
Spirit employs a system of "master and slave" robots, in which one on the inside, like the one seen here, works in tandem with another one on the outside, each tracking the other as they drill holes and add small components.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/0516f9d8-9bbd-44a5-91df-6245ff69e802/thumbnail/770x578/b155cbff3bd6a04266418cd8ec1fce2e/section-on-truck.jpg
A 737 side section, which includes a number of windows, sits on a trailer, awaiting further work by Spirit Aerosystems technicians.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/24/0d72cce9-3eec-48d9-9371-3a1d400d0ad2/thumbnail/770x578/85b6a514bc82cc64aa5e58878d912dc5/fuselage.jpg
