[Date]2014-07-30
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/43a60444-466a-42b1-8ed2-545a40db67ac/thumbnail/770x578/b48e167da081a1ac26d33d733a40a91c/baracuda-and-the-rig.jpg
In the Gulf of Mexico, from oil rigs to fish havens
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/debde018-c8d3-4913-a1cc-320f2ca09e09/thumbnail/770x578/bd5a4ab33cf40cfd739d455138a5737b/looking-up-to-top-1.jpg
Most of the decommissioned rigs have their platforms severed, and only begin at 85 feet below the surface. This rig, technically known as a production platform, is the High Island 389. Owned by W&amp;T Offshote, it's under consideration for donation to the Texas Rigs to Reefs program. As of today, it has not had its platform severed but it is considered officially idle.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/8db5d08d-59d7-4e4f-9df7-1ef1612f75d7/thumbnail/770x578/e8dde7989dd32612d727f3e74f0e3604/rig-from-the-surface.jpg
High Island 389, seen from the surface of the Gulf of Mexico.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/a2273e42-4dd6-4f23-a3a6-e6b0f477ab8e/thumbnail/770x578/5dad6804b8e75dd012b3ab137b9db7f7/tons-of-fish-2.jpg
It's estimated that each of the artificial reefs in the program can be home to between 12,000 and 14,000 fish. The High Island 389, while not yet part of the program, is already home to teeming marine life.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/0c693e19-4511-4c32-86ac-39202e27eb65/thumbnail/770x578/d1b0404e1af9df26326500d1e4d87c1b/divers-investigating.jpg
The Rigs to Reefs program creates new habitats for marine life and also offers new opportunities for fishing and scuba diving.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/dd16d1b1-573e-4c28-8b57-017be5f50c07/thumbnail/770x578/ff1193b5f51f42d8b0d7fbc661b9b734/selfie.jpg
CNET reporter Daniel Terdiman waves hello in a selfie taken within the perimeter of High Island 389.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/fb1c9eda-7f30-4deb-95f5-feb026f8e9d2/thumbnail/770x578/5459810f540335143a53aa74e3f948d8/fish-at-the-rig.jpg
Many species of fish call High Island 389 their home. It's not yet clear what will happen to the oil rig, which is currently "idle," according to W&amp;T Offshore, the company that owns it.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/2bd9408f-f379-4991-b850-ea84fc98e73d/thumbnail/770x578/6a1c976d9cfbdb5d157a3a467189983e/officialbarracuda.jpg
A barracuda swims within a decommissioned oil rig in this official Texas Rigs to Reefs program photo.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/a2a8e4d7-852e-40b7-8af2-71f270007c8f/thumbnail/770x578/5e37aa571685d01e8b463ffbda6ce143/7-3frenchangel.jpg
A fish known as a French Angel calls this decommissioned oil rig -- not High Island 389 -- home.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/edfa2c40-c5cb-4bc5-9ec9-278dbdb817e6/thumbnail/770x578/decb7e57fd961b7fd90f98f49bb8f50f/7-3spotfinbutterfly.jpg
Another species of fish that calls the Gulf of Mexico, and this decommissioned oil rig, home is the Spotfin Butterfly
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/9b81187f-efaa-4df4-b602-9c0a90b8d7b7/thumbnail/770x578/f699371ef53ee5d4abacc9db3a4c4972/7-3spanishhogfish.jpg
A number of Spanish Hogfish brighten the area inside this decommissioned oil rig.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/625c1cae-bdab-4b36-b8c4-0b2554114c5d/thumbnail/770x578/7062e59cf96d705f319695d5fd2cf8c7/7-3spadefish.jpg
Looking up toward the top of the High Island 389, you'll see hundreds, if not thousands, of fish.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/be67b467-99a6-41eb-8e5a-d397e27fb95e/thumbnail/770x578/22e8173c99cf1c953bff3eafa23de7c6/fish-down-below-1.jpg
The average decommissioned oil rig has piles -- legs -- that go down 200 feet or more below the surface. The High Island 389, which is not yet part of the Rigs to Reefs program, goes down 300 feet, and fish can be found all the way down -- though most of those depths are below the range of recreational scuba divers.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/19152178-c2a5-44a1-acf6-89a8fab5d981/thumbnail/770x578/9b838816770429f94ad6bc13c1326113/fish-and-a-joint.jpg
A major joint in the High Island 389 platform is teeming with fish.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/b725d205-68e4-440f-a4a6-18df4a29c58a/thumbnail/770x578/6f0d286778e7bba31938801f682b21c6/fish-and-a-beam.jpg
This beam, part of the High Island 389 production platform, is covered in marine life.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/199ce3fe-1fb9-45f6-9130-a25a23712a96/thumbnail/770x578/93b6182180ecfda5f678b0785e08e0e8/highland-389-from-far-away.jpg
The High Island 389 disappears into the distance.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/9fa8bed5-405e-4cd5-97dc-b8d72a17368d/thumbnail/770x578/df2776800e1efd8e8e605fe197152b41/growth-on-a-beam.jpg
Marine life is abundant within the perimeter of the High Island 389.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/682b7305-b70b-4d7d-87d2-dd512836d304/thumbnail/770x578/c92596f4779f44ae39b643733a66ae34/fish-down-below.jpg
Teeming marine life in the depths of the High Island 389 production platform.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/07/29/5b0c4d65-6df9-4054-97ae-4c27d6dd6714/thumbnail/770x578/1e65e3c8f7ccdcb26d70304a7dcddf86/official-looking-up.jpg
A look straight up at the underside of the main part of a production platform in the Gulf of Mexico.
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Date]2014-08-12
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/d6fbc599-5024-43f6-bf7a-4ae5a27859d4/thumbnail/770x578/6451d93a87eb80f297ecd7f06a6a562c/eco-silo.jpg
Town goes all green after devastating tornado 
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/246edaa1-8d0f-4500-9984-768ff24ed764/thumbnail/770x578/fc720b92a562574ba75642a2b99a45ca/tornado-photo.png
An aerial look at Greensburg in the wake of the May 4, 2007, tornado that destroyed 95 percent of the small Kansas town's buildings and killed 12 people.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/60250e67-9c91-49a9-a6ea-2c599d81b768/thumbnail/770x578/8d74e0d53f0249277dc43c0600443573/greensburg-house-outline.jpg
In this photo, taken using a DJI Phantom 2 Vision-plus, it's possible to see the Silo Eco-Home (left) as well as a former home site (lower right) that has yet to be rebuilt on. It's possible to see the outline of the original house located on the property, still visible in the overgrown grass.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/71ada015-dab4-4097-a18d-3df8050bd55e/thumbnail/770x578/17dd688d2cb396e21c229173fdcb185f/city-hall-commons-from-air.jpg
In this aerial photo, shot using a DJI Phantom 2 Vision-plus, the roofs of Greensburg's City Hall (left) and County Commons are visible. Both buildings were build using green principles, and are LEED-certified.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/43301c60-2636-41b2-a079-2bd142a10cac/thumbnail/770x578/6f0f2242ccf18c81e2da927116c362cc/arts-center.jpg
The 5.4.7 Arts Center -- named for the date of the tornado -- is a LEED-certified building in Greensburg built with reclaimed wood, and featuring many other green elements. Greensburg has 11 LEED-certified buildings.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/e360011e-4a3a-4eb3-b773-9b988b379f16/thumbnail/770x578/f26738979847bbab317c080b6d2f51cc/school.jpg
The all-new Kiowa County Schools, in Greensburg, is a sustainable building complex housing the county's entire school system. It features a wide variety of sustainable elements, such as large windows that let in lots of natural light, bleachers made from recycled milk and water jugs, rainwater catchment systems, and much more.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/3161c654-d7da-4a1f-ae85-cd1e403b5848/thumbnail/770x578/f879b7f3fc73291275c1b19e9eed9e5a/greensburg-wind-speeds-map.png
A map showing the tornado's wind speeds as it rolled through Greensburg. The strongest winds -- more than 200 miles an hour -- hit the center of town. All told, the tornado was measured at 1.7 miles wide.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/177753e8-5dd9-4091-a80a-51a1afa050ee/thumbnail/770x578/391f42f67ff7938706faf94078b1ca72/city-hall.jpg
A look at Greensburg's all-new City Hall.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/bce4e8e8-ca08-4ab4-9a52-b735086d6ac3/thumbnail/770x578/faf891c1ade474423f1a63cae945933b/remnants.jpg
The remnants of a pre-tornado building, still visible in the center of Greensburg.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/3c3d11a5-2061-4f04-812e-cf675c091b0a/thumbnail/770x578/42ef10b74f8c6b24fc113357cb82c6b6/grain-silo.jpg
Although nearly all of Greensburg's buildings were destroyed by the tornado, the town's grain silo was still standing when the storm passed. It became a model for the type of structure that could survive an EF-5 tornado.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/74ddd3ff-2db9-41c6-8129-c2100a761b8a/thumbnail/770x578/c320e4d47a8a9b5fde552cd0ff1c8a15/green-roof.jpg
A living roof on top of the County Commons building provides a number of green benefits, including rainwater absorption and natural cooling.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/30d0eded-a9be-4ed0-823a-c392e06834cf/thumbnail/770x578/959e6af047c284d66f77a5ef62105186/water-catchment.jpg
A water catchment system at the County Schools complex in Greensburg, Kan.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/ae49dbc6-938a-4b4d-895c-7bd59bf0a277/thumbnail/770x578/13b515c12b1394ab66d1076f38111b85/locker-room.jpg
The locker room inside the County Schools complex was partially funded with federal money intended for building storm shelters. By placing the locker room inside the shelter, the school board was able to take advantage of "creative financing."
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/05/685c81bd-4de9-4195-8897-e6b45055cf5b/thumbnail/770x578/41435b2aec7cd8bbb62a67e7262cb5bf/the-big-well.jpg
One of Greensburg's main attractions, the so-called "Big Well," as seen from a DJI Phantom 2 Vision-plus.
 
 
 
 
 
[Date]2014-08-13
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/594105ea-f83a-4d8f-a40c-03ae087033c8/thumbnail/770x578/1564b71435928af3487e74f9c9fecc2c/320-million-dollars.jpg
$320 Million Bills
It's hard to know how you're going to feel starting at $320 million in cash.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/648f4a62-c15e-4b86-9e02-0df8e9cca037/thumbnail/770x578/87a0d219ae695464e37691b5f479dcd8/electroplating-quick-wash-with-silver-nitrate.jpg
One of the earliest stages of the production process is known as electroplating.In this part of the process, technicians take a plastic master sheet, known as a "basso," and, as seen here, spray it with silver nitrate, which serves as an electrical conductor, according to the Bureau of Engraving and Printing.The plate is submerged in a tank of nickel salt solution, and electrical current is added. At that point, nickel ions transfer from the solution to the surface of the master, which is electrically charged.The plate is left in the tank for 22 hours, after which a nickel plate, known as an "alto," has literally grown.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/164864da-9c0c-44ef-b9a7-17e947f654c1/thumbnail/770x578/4fbc538ca6de4103d38072060c0ea90b/electroplating-dropping-in-solution.jpg
Here, we see a Bureau of Engraving and Printing technician dropping the plastic master plate into the nickel salt solution.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/9adbcf97-883a-48f9-b6b0-f2da7c4c1242/thumbnail/770x578/4cee3fc9997495239683513e91ebc8b4/electroplating-grown-alto-plate.jpg
This is an "alto," a nickel plate that has literally grown onto the surface of the plastic master after 22 hours in the nickel salt solution.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/4d19fde1-4537-4cee-9b82-efa36349ef80/thumbnail/770x578/07e5fc605f6d13ba407148e40bc72f51/electroplating-alto-separated-from-master.jpg
After technicians pull the plate out of the solution, they physically separate the alto from the plastic master. The alto is a perfect negative image of the original plastic master plate.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/4100907e-61ed-4a22-8299-dbfc4772989c/thumbnail/770x578/142ac1043d38a97ffbde1cf4c74f2a73/tracing-numbers.jpg
In the facility's engraving department, a team of engravers etch many of the features of the $100 bill into steel dies, making what were originally designers' models into 3D engravings. To do so, they employ tools known as gravers, as well as acids.Complicating matters, the engravers must etch all the features in reverse, since the dies will be pressed onto a plate.Each engraver works on different elements of the notes. Seen here, an engraver is etching numbers, which are then automatically transferred by a pantograph onto a plate that will be used in the printing process.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/a657b1fb-0428-46b5-a875-9046f57eeb14/thumbnail/770x578/fcdf4a8df2bf14fbf8c64916471a3ead/pantographing-numbers.jpg
A pantograph transfers the engraver's etchings onto each note on a plate.
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/5780b38a-8ff6-48c7-8f32-37ee4b5d1b23/thumbnail/770x578/7f44e6a169f9936129e7fd096e39b649/inspecting-at-engraving.jpg
Using a magnifying glass, an engraver inspects a plate for any kind of defect.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/d2d1d582-058e-4b84-81c4-a1e69d994ced/thumbnail/770x578/464902174df339d334a946febd927a44/numbers-engraved-on-plate.jpg
In the lower left hand corner of the right-hand note on this plate, you can see the reverse image of the number 346, which has just been added by a pantograph after an engraver etched it.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/0aa81064-3494-4f23-b902-5c461ce2cc8a/thumbnail/770x578/64c940a4d0721ab2a269a38af8d811a2/tools-of-the-trade.jpg
These are an engraver's 'tools of the trade,' many of which are hand-made by the engraver, or passed down from generation to generation. The tools can sometimes be 100 years old.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/8b7c5d27-5113-4646-b430-21c9d9bc58d2/thumbnail/770x578/a4028d08b93bfa4a796ab4eba25b9b13/chromed.jpg
After being pantographed, plates have chrome added in order to increase their longevity, meaning they can be used again and again in the printing process.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/085d6d1d-dac4-43f6-9661-9ccd321f379a/thumbnail/770x578/9de14ada9a1e58a7b69389f1e970f263/chromed-plate-at-inspection.jpg
After having the yellow solution washed off, a chrome plate is held up for inspection.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/6580b814-3417-4c06-8cad-049725852562/thumbnail/770x578/3bbdd6ac490f0675f86b30eee0651307/single-subject-at-photo-engraving.jpg
In the Western Currency Facility's photo-engraving department, technicians use computers to design specific elements of the notes, such as a feather and inkwell from the back side of the $100 bill, which are then printed onto film.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/a61d0685-9d3c-46a2-82bd-d8d55ea1e548/thumbnail/770x578/8f12d547107d5dc63c850d8e94f7f80f/photographing-film-one-color-at-a-time.jpg
The film is then exposed, one color at a time -- blue, copper, tan, and yellow -- to an image setting machine. Each film is one color.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/ff90c3af-1b7c-4b64-aad1-bbb596a97822/thumbnail/770x578/072a016e57bb2cfaeb5a770bc488a12b/plate-after-filming.jpg
A plate, like the one seen here, is generated based on the photographs taken by the image setter. That plate is then put into a printing press.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/a314301a-542b-47fb-8125-4e48e0862928/thumbnail/770x578/32d6d2822beb90bb29eb28a5e081bdb0/plates-on-printing-press.jpg
A printing press, with two plates on rollers, which add specific elements of the $100 bill, like the inkwell, and feather.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/580a9bfb-62d2-4552-a065-2c95767f4299/thumbnail/770x578/369f8f103bc359170b2d9c3bafb0b380/checking-the-watermark.jpg
A sheet with several elements already printed is examined on a light table to make sure the notes' watermarks are in the right place.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/5e11cccd-4b40-4245-a873-983a854ec637/thumbnail/770x578/441e2afaac0e6f738a2500001c9cf5ee/printing-sheets-1.jpg
The front sides of 32-note sheets are printed as they make their way through this printing press. First one side, then the other is printed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/dfd542de-52d4-4d40-b25c-c2feb665f038/thumbnail/770x578/b22971568e3cd42080a589ed5cc0eecc/many-stacks-of-currency-drying.jpg
Countless stacks of currency sit and dry for 72 hours, before they are brought back to the printing process in order to have their back sides printed.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/b4f325d5-4629-4df4-b14a-a5aa4fd1cd30/thumbnail/770x578/d9871e01415e369b202cf5f3b6d4b56d/printed-backs-in-the-printer.jpg
The back sides of the sheets have now been printed.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/f00aa99d-4d62-4fb7-a755-9e636d0fbffd/thumbnail/770x578/8049c1556902a62b2c94210c3ce3ecdd/inspecting-rear-of-sheets.jpg
A technician uses a magnifying glass to inspect the back side of this sheet of $100 bills, looking for any kind of defect. If he finds any defects, the sheets are removed and destroyed.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/3e4e5042-a17b-45bb-8e87-f8ad9e83139c/thumbnail/770x578/01df17de4ec09e20070fd8e7b67f37f5/jogger.jpg
A technician uses the "jogger," a machine that blows air into the stacks of bills after they've dried for 72 hours. He also uses his hands to separate them.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/9e29e02e-22a5-4849-80dd-7466df1e81b9/thumbnail/770x578/5b2720ddb82a4af32cbe7594daa48f16/holding-full-and-half-sheet.jpg
Two Western Currency Facility technicians hold up sheets of $100 bills. On the left side, we see a sheet that has been cut into two halves, while a full 32-note sheet is seen on the right.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/f919cbb3-235d-4272-baf3-cf99ca6121dd/thumbnail/770x578/174ffd0f69c741539d32308bc06eaf4c/camera-inspecting-for-defects.jpg
As 32-note sheets come off the press, a camera inspects them, looking for any defects. If they're detected, the sheets are automatically removed.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/eb91ff8d-5ee6-4f36-a40b-a0670bce0514/thumbnail/770x578/50a847f5e57a3e046eb1b63d3407bfc4/cutting-32-to-16.jpg
A machine slices a 32-note sheet in two 16-note halves.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/bd875800-3c53-4cc1-96dd-ef24deadf37e/thumbnail/770x578/058f7712a894285bb9da9558f93a5721/cut-from-16-to-2.jpg
A slicer then cuts the 16-note sheets into sets of two notes.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/27d4654f-4594-4369-a438-48196abe5790/thumbnail/770x578/34544a131c04f12003bd044f251c13ef/separated-into-single-stacks.jpg
Finally, another slicer cuts the notes into stacks of single notes.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/c184fce6-43ea-42de-bf9c-875e38616bbb/thumbnail/770x578/4acc3900319c652a4654bfb94787b7cd/straps.jpg
A machine collates "straps," as stacks of 100 $100 bills are known.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/5a0ebcd4-ef7b-4c8b-9574-47393e800fa8/thumbnail/770x578/679077ad1c42c12286efa4efa0f99199/bundles-in-a-carousel.jpg
Each slot in this carousel holds a "bundle," or 10 straps of $100 bills. Each bundle is $100,000.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/0ca5f21d-d110-426b-80e4-241b7ae5dd5c/thumbnail/770x578/d640e705fb90163b68ee3f9f490505f8/bundle.jpg
A bundle of $100 bills, or $100,000.
 
http://cnet2.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/809a9622-03cb-4cc7-adeb-f5b4db7f5b50/thumbnail/770x578/713d7798e91491fd8a7f9705e7e0798f/shrink-wrapped-brick.jpg
A shrink-wrapped brick of $100 bills, or four bundles, totaling $400,000.
 
http://cnet1.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/ffbe501a-d99a-4d78-89bb-5ecd4fac9efa/thumbnail/770x578/3b5003b83eb40cfd9feec21c3d8f85c3/headed-for-san-francisco.jpg
Stacks of packaged $100 bills are seen at the Western Currency Facility in Fort Worth, Texas. These bills are destined for the Federal Reserve Bank in San Francisco.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/1e0ef411-b0be-4be8-b105-fc269a6a8107/thumbnail/770x578/77b6828018b4ae681a168d53e06913c3/old-and-new-sheets.jpg
Western Currency Facility plant manager Charlene Williams (left) and a fellow Bureau of Engraving and Printing employee show off a 50-subject sheet of $1 bills -- which the facility now prints -- and an old 32-note sheet. The facility is currently only printing 50-subject $1 bills, but plans to expand to other denominations soon.
 
http://cnet4.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/9df6a375-9a05-4127-b09b-f498fd09a293/thumbnail/770x578/96432e1aafc68ff2067d2c45f73dbae5/anti-counterfeit-1.png
A look at the color-shifting inkwell and 3D security ribbon, the two new anti-counterfeiting features being used on $100 bills.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/78b65d06-e488-4f7a-a493-9ab9874b7fe2/thumbnail/770x578/cf0924396a0c1418f2991830d2a0a5a7/anti-counterfeit-2.png
A look at the anti-counterfeiting features from a different angle.
 
http://cnet3.cbsistatic.com/hub/i/r/2014/08/12/63dbd2dc-26d0-49fb-8b79-a49bf2f81ee8/thumbnail/770x578/a8e107fbd3a1f18eff1df93c251e78ef/tiny-print.jpg
The $100 bill features many anti-counterfeiting measures, including tiny print that is invisible to the naked eye, and which is extremely difficult to reproduce. In this image, the letters "USA" are repeated again and again on the lower edge of the note, and the words "United States of America" are repeated on Benjamin Franklin's collar.
